---
title: L8Log
client: Remote Tech
dateRange: November 2019 - January 2026
startDate: November 2019
endDate: January 2026
role: Senior Front-End Engineer (Contract)
summary: L8Log is a comprehensive IoT remote monitoring and compliance system for Legionella control. I led the front-end development and was primarily responsible for architectural decisions, UI/UX implementation, and technology migrations. I built and maintained a large React application focused on operational workflows, access control, performance, and reliability
nda: true
highlights:
  - Designed a centralised authorisation policy used across routes and UI controls
  - Improved UX consistency with reusable layout and empty-state primitives
  - Implemented robust data-fetching patterns with RTK Query and an Axios baseQuery
stack:
  - React
  - TypeScript
  - Redux Toolkit / RTK Query
  - Tailwind CSS
  - Vite
  - ECharts / Ant Design Charts
  - Mapbox
  - Playwright
outcomes:
  - Faster iteration through clearer architecture and shared UI patterns
  - Reduced regressions through improved determinism and guard rails around access and behaviour

<!-- ## Media

This work was delivered under NDA.

- Screenshots and recordings are redacted to remove customer data, identifiers, and internal URLs
- A fuller walkthrough can be shared privately on request

### What to capture (NDA-safe)

- Login screen only (no credentials)
- Navigation and information architecture (sidebar/tabs), with any site or customer names blurred
- List pages with filters/search/sort/pagination (blur table rows)
- Empty states (blank slates) and loading states (skeletons/spinners)
- A modal open/close interaction (no submit), showing focus management and keyboard navigation
- Responsiveness: the same page at desktop and mobile widths

### What to avoid

- Customer-identifying data (names, addresses, IDs, company numbers)
- Internal URLs, domains, API hosts, and any auth provider screens
- Any create/update/delete submission or anything that looks like a production write action -->

<!-- ## What I built

- Authorisation policy and feature access gating
- Route composition and page layout structure
- Shared UI primitives for navigation, empty states, and data tables
- API layer patterns for consistent request behaviour

## How I work

- Start with user journeys and failure modes
- Prefer small composable components with clear ownership
- Treat accessibility and performance as product features -->
